ğŸš¨ Using Real Brands (like Bud Light) in Cartoons:

Short answer: ğŸ‘‰ You technically can't use a real brand name/logo like "Bud Light" without permission if you're using it for commercial purposes (like selling the show, merch, YouTube ads, etc.).

----------------------

âœï¸ Here's Why:

Trademarks protect brand names, logos, and recognizable packaging.

Even if you're not "hurting" Bud Light, using their exact name/logo without permission could theoretically cause a legal issue once the show gets big.

If it stays small/fan project level â€” companies usually donâ€™t care.

If it blows up (and yours could), you wanna be 100% clean and safe.

----------------------

ğŸ¯ Best Solution: Use a "Fake Brand" that's obviously a parody.

(This is what Family Guy, Rick & Morty, The Simpsons, etc., do ALL THE TIME.)

Example ideas:

Real Brand Gator Grove Version

Bud Light Bub Light / Bud Latt / Mud Light

Busch Bushwhack / Boosh

Coors Light Cooterâ€™s Light (lol perfect)

Â· You just change the name slightly.

Â· Keep the can same vibe (blue/silver color), so people instantly get the joke.

It's parody â€” legally protected. (And funnier anyway!) ----------------------

ğŸ§  Parody Protection = Your Best Friend

In the U.S., parody is a legally protected form of free speech, even against big companies â€” As long as it's a joke and not trying to "confuse consumers" into thinking it's real Bud Light advertising.
